pattern 1/832: PROVED cells=13 depth=2 diamonds=1 odd_wheels=0 circular_ladders=0 bridged_hexagons=0 set_equivalences=1 parity_transports=0 pigeonhole_xwings=1 branches=0 complete=true greedy_branches=0 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=0 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=0 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0
000000000000000000000000000000000000000001001001000011000001110001000001011001000
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r7c6, r7c7, r7c8, r8c9} (spine r7c7—r7c8).
      → color(r7c6) = color(r8c9). Identify.
  2.  SET: {row 6, row 9} − {col 3, col 9}.
      Remainder: {r6c8, r9c2, r9c6} = {r5c9, [r7c6=r8c9], r8c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c6, r5c9, r6c8, r9c6}:
      Diagonals: {r5c6, r6c8} and {r5c9, r9c6} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r5c6) = color(r6c8) → forces r5c9 = r6c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r5c9) = color(r9c6) → forces r5c9 = r8c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

000000000000000000000000000000000000000001001001000011000001110001000001110001000
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r7c6, r7c7, r7c8, r8c9} (spine r7c7—r7c8).
      → color(r7c6) = color(r8c9). Identify.
  2.  SET: {row 6, row 7, row 9} − {box 6, box 7, box 9}.
      Remainder: {r6c3, [r7c6=r8c9], r9c6} = {r5c9, [r7c6=r8c9], r8c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  Odd wheel: hub [r7c6=r8c9] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r5c6, r5c9, r6c9, r6c3, r9c6} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

pattern 10/832: PROVED cells=13 depth=2 diamonds=2 odd_wheels=0 circular_ladders=0 bridged_hexagons=1 set_equivalences=0 parity_transports=0 pigeonhole_xwings=0 branches=0 complete=true greedy_branches=0 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=0 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=0 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0
000000000000000000000000000000000000000001001001000110000001011001000001011001000
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c9, r6c7, r6c8, r6c3} (spine r6c7—r6c8).
      → color(r5c9) = color(r6c3). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {[r5c9=r6c3], r7c9, r8c9, r7c8} (spine r7c9—r8c9).
      → color([r5c9=r6c3]) = color(r7c8). Identify.
  3.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r7c6, r7c9, r8c9, r8c3, r9c2, r9c6}
      Bridges: [r5c9=r6c3=r7c8]—r9c3 (edges r7c6—r7c9 ↔ r8c3—r9c2), [r5c9=r6c3=r7c8]—r9c3 (edges r7c9—r8c9 ↔ r9c2—r9c6), [r5c9=r6c3=r7c8]—r5c6 (edges r8c9—r8c3 ↔ r9c6—r7c6).
      Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
      but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  3.  Diamond {r8c3, [r6c3=r7c6], r9c3, r9c5} (spine [r6c3=r7c6]—r9c3).
      → color(r8c3) = color(r9c5). Identify.
  4.  K₄ on {[r8c3=r9c5], r8c7, r8c8, r9c7}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  1.  Diamond {r8c3, r9c1, r9c2, r9c8} (spine r9c1—r9c2).
      → color(r8c3) = color(r9c8). Identify.
  2.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c8, r6c9, r6c3, [r8c3=r9c8]}:
      Diagonals: {r5c8, r6c3} and {r6c9, [r8c3=r9c8]} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r5c8) = color(r6c3) → forces r7c6 = r7c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r6c9) = color([r8c3=r9c8]) → forces r5c6 = r7c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c6, r5c8, r5c9, r6c9} (spine r5c8—r5c9).
      → color(r5c6) = color(r6c9). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c3, [r5c6=r6c9], r6c6, r7c6} (spine [r5c6=r6c9]—r6c6).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  3.  SET: {row 7, row 9} − {box 7, box 9}.
      Remainder: {[r6c3=r7c6]} = {r8c3}.
      → color([r6c3=r7c6]) = color(r8c3), but they share a house. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Diamond {r6c3, [r5c6=r6c7], r6c6, r7c6} (spine [r5c6=r6c7]—r6c6).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r8c5, r8c9, r9c7, r9c5}:
      Diagonals: {r8c5, r9c7} and {r8c9, r9c5} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r8c5) = color(r9c7) → forces [r6c3=r7c6] = r8c5 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c9) = color(r9c5) → forces [r6c3=r7c6] = r9c5 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → color(r5c6) = color(r6c7). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c3, [r5c6=r6c7], r6c6, r9c6} (spine [r5c6=r6c7]—r6c6).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r9c6). Identify.
  3.  SET: {row 8, row 9} − {box 7, box 9}.
      Remainder: {[r6c3=r9c6]} = {r7c3}.
      → color([r6c3=r9c6]) = color(r7c3), but they share a house. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

000000000000000000000000000000000000001001001001010010000000001001010010010001100
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r5c9, r8c8:
      Case A: color(r5c9) = color(r8c8). Identify.
        2.  Diamond {r5c6, r5c3, [r5c9=r8c8], r8c3} (spine r5c3—[r5c9=r8c8]).
            → color(r5c6) = color(r8c3). Identify.
        3.  Odd wheel: hub [r5c6=r8c3] forces rim to 2 colors.
            Bivalue oddagon {r5c3, [r5c9=r8c8], r8c5, r6c5, r6c3} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r5c9) ≠ color(r8c8). Add edge.
        4.  Diamond {r6c8, r5c9, r8c8, r7c9} (spine r5c9—r8c8).
            → color(r6c8) = color(r7c9). Identify.
        5.  Parity transport:
            row 5 {r5c3, r5c6, r5c9}
            row 6 {r6c3, r6c5, [r6c8=r7c9]}
            row 8 {r8c3, r8c5, r8c8}
            row 9 {r9c2, r9c6, r9c7}
            Parallel links: row 5↔row 6 (col, box, box); row 6↔row 8 (col, col, col); row 8↔row 9 (box, box, box)
            → same permutation parity.
            Each pair shares a column → distinct permutations.
            4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

        4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c6, r5c9, r6c8, r6c5}:
            Diagonals: {r5c6, r6c8} and {r5c9, r6c5} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c6) = color(r6c8) → forces r5c6 = r7c3 (adjacent). Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r5c9) = color(r6c5) → forces r6c5 = r9c5 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  1.  Diamond {r6c8, r4c9, r5c9, r7c9} (spine r4c9—r5c9).

  2.  Diamond {r5c6, r6c4, r6c5, [r6c8=r7c9]} (spine r6c4—r6c5).
      → color(r5c6) = color([r6c8=r7c9]). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r8c3, r8c8, r9c7, r9c3}:
      Diagonals: {r8c3, r9c7} and {r8c8, r9c3} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r8c3) = color(r9c7) → forces [r5c6=r6c8=r7c9] = r9c7 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c8) = color(r9c3) → forces [r5c6=r6c8=r7c9] = r8c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Bridges: r9c8—r9c3 (edges [r5c6=r9c5]—r5c8 ↔ r6c3—r8c3), r4c9—r8c9 (edges r5c8—r6c7 ↔ r8c3—r8c6), r7c7—r7c6 (edges r6c7—r6c3 ↔ r8c6—[r5c6=r9c5]).

      but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  3.  Odd wheel: hub [r6c7=r7c6] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r4c9, r5c8, r5c6, r6c5, r6c3} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3, r9c2} (spine r7c3—r8c3).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r9c2). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c7, [r6c3=r9c2], r9c7, r9c6} (spine [r6c3=r9c2]—r9c7).
      → color(r6c7) = color(r9c6). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r5c8, r5c6, [r6c7=r9c6], r6c5} (spine r5c6—[r6c7=r9c6]).
      → color(r5c8) = color(r6c5). Identify.
  4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r6c3=r9c2], r8c3, r8c9, r9c7}:
      Diagonals: {[r6c3=r9c2], r8c9} and {r8c3, r9c7} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r6c3=r9c2]) = color(r8c9) → forces r4c9 = r8c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c3) = color(r9c7) → forces r5c6 = [r5c8=r6c5] (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  3.  SET: {row 8, row 9} − {box 7, box 9}.
      Remainder: {[r3c9=r6c8=r8c6]} = {r7c8}.
      → color([r3c9=r6c8=r8c6]) = color(r7c8), but they share a house. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → color(r8c3) = color(r9c8). Identify.
  2.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r5c9, r6c7, r6c6, r8c6, [r8c3=r9c8], r7c9}
      Bridges: r6c8—r8c8 (edges r5c9—r6c7 ↔ r8c6—[r8c3=r9c8]), r6c8—r8c8 (edges r6c7—r6c6 ↔ [r8c3=r9c8]—r7c9), r3c6—r3c9 (edges r6c6—r8c6 ↔ r7c9—r5c9).

  1.  Diamond {r5c9, r6c7, r6c8, r6c6} (spine r6c7—r6c8).
      → color(r5c9) = color(r6c6). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r3c9, r3c6, [r5c9=r6c6], r7c6} (spine r3c6—[r5c9=r6c6]).
      → color(r3c9) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  3.  SET: {row 8, row 9} − {box 7, box 8}.
      Remainder: {r8c9} = {[r3c9=r7c6]}.
      → color(r8c9) = color([r3c9=r7c6]), but they share a house. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Case 1: color([r3c6=r8c7]) = color(r9c3) → forces r5c9 = r6c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c3) = color(r9c9) → forces [r3c9=r6c6=r7c8] = r9c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  1.  Circular ladder {r8c3—r9c3, r8c6—r9c6, r8c9—r9c8}:
      Satellites r6c3 (rung 1), r3c6 (rung 2), r7c9 (rung 3) forced to distinct colors. Add triangle.
  2.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c6, r6c3, r8c3, r8c6}:
      Diagonals: {r3c6, r8c3} and {r6c3, r8c6} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r3c6) = color(r8c3) → forces r3c6 = r3c9 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r6c3) = color(r8c6) → forces r5c8 = r9c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

pattern 395/832: PROVED cells=13 depth=2 diamonds=1 odd_wheels=0 circular_ladders=0 bridged_hexagons=0 set_equivalences=1 parity_transports=0 pigeonhole_xwings=1 branches=0 complete=true greedy_branches=0 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=0 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=0 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0
000000000000000000000001001000000000001000110001001010000000001000000001001001100
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r3c9, r7c9, r8c9, r9c7} (spine r7c9—r8c9).
      → color(r3c9) = color(r9c7). Identify.
  2.  SET: {row 6, row 9} − {col 3, col 6}.
      Remainder: {[r3c9=r9c7], r6c8} = {r3c6, r5c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c6, [r3c9=r9c7], r5c7, r5c3}:
      Diagonals: {r3c6, r5c7} and {[r3c9=r9c7], r5c3} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r3c6) = color(r5c7) → forces r3c6 = [r3c9=r9c7] (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color([r3c9=r9c7]) = color(r5c3) → forces [r3c9=r9c7] = r6c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  4.  Odd wheel: hub [r4c9=r6c6=r9c8] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r3c6, r3c9, r9c9, [r6c3=r9c2], r6c8, r5c8, r5c6} (length 7) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  SET: {row 5, row 9} − {col 3, col 9}.

      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c6, r3c9, r6c3, r6c6}:
      Diagonals: {r3c6, r6c3} and {r3c9, r6c6} (non-adjacent).

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → color(r3c9) = color(r9c8). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {[r3c6=r9c5], r3c8, [r3c9=r9c8], r6c8} (spine r3c8—[r3c9=r9c8]).
      → color([r3c6=r9c5]) = color(r6c8). Identify.
  4.  Parity transport:
      row 3 {[r3c6=r6c8=r9c5], r3c8, [r3c9=r9c8]}
      row 6 {r6c3, [r3c6=r6c8=r9c5], r6c9}
      row 8 {r8c3, r8c6, r8c9}
      row 9 {r9c2, [r3c6=r6c8=r9c5], [r3c9=r9c8]}
      Parallel links: row 3↔row 6 (box, col, col); row 6↔row 8 (col, box, col); row 8↔row 9 (box, box, box)
      → same permutation parity.
      Each pair shares a column → distinct permutations.
      4 same-parity permutations from 3 available → pigeonhole contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r8c3, r9c1, r9c2, r9c6} (spine r9c1—r9c2).
      → color(r8c3) = color(r9c6). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c9, r6c3, r6c6, [r8c3=r9c6]} (spine r6c3—r6c6).
      → color(r6c9) = color([r8c3=r9c6]). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r3c8, r3c6, r3c9, [r6c9=r8c3=r9c6]} (spine r3c6—r3c9).
      → color(r3c8) = color([r6c9=r8c3=r9c6]). Identify.
  4.  K₄ on {[r3c8=r6c9=r8c3=r9c6], r7c8, r7c9, r8c7}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

000000000000000000000001011000000000000000000001001001000001000001000011001010010
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {row 3, row 6, row 8, row 9} − {col 3, col 6, col 8, col 9}.
      Remainder: {r9c5} = {r7c6}.
      → color(r9c5) = color(r7c6), but they share a house. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

pattern 494/832: PROVED cells=13 depth=2 diamonds=2 odd_wheels=0 circular_ladders=0 bridged_hexagons=0 set_equivalences=0 parity_transports=0 pigeonhole_xwings=1 branches=0 complete=true greedy_branches=0 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=0 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=0 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0
000000000000000000000001011000000000000000000001001001000001000001000011001110000
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r7c6, r9c4, r9c5, r9c3} (spine r9c4—r9c5).
      → color(r7c6) = color(r9c3). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c9, r6c3, r6c6, [r7c6=r9c3]} (spine r6c3—r6c6).
      → color(r6c9) = color([r7c6=r9c3]). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c8, r3c9, r8c9, r8c8}:
      Diagonals: {r3c8, r8c9} and {r3c9, r8c8} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r3c8) = color(r8c9) → forces r6c3 = r6c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r3c9) = color(r8c8) → forces r6c3 = r6c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c3, r8c3, r9c3, r9c2} (spine r8c3—r9c3).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r9c2). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r7c6, r8c4, r8c5, r8c3} (spine r8c4—r8c5).
      → color(r7c6) = color(r8c3). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r3c6, r6c6, [r7c6=r8c3], [r6c3=r9c2]} (spine r6c6—[r7c6=r8c3]).
      → color(r3c6) = color([r6c3=r9c2]). Identify.
  4.  Odd wheel: hub [r3c6=r6c3=r9c2] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r3c8, r3c9, r6c9, r6c6, [r7c6=r8c3], r9c3, r9c8} (length 7) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  3.  Diamond {[r3c9=r7c8=r9c6], r6c6, r6c9, r6c3} (spine r6c6—r6c9).
      → color([r3c9=r7c8=r9c6]) = color(r6c3). Identify.
  4.  K₄ on {[r3c9=r6c3=r7c8=r9c6], r8c3, r9c2, r9c3}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r3c9, r5c9, r6c9, r6c8} (spine r5c9—r6c9).
      → color(r3c9) = color(r6c8). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r3c6, r3c8, [r3c9=r6c8], r8c8} (spine r3c8—[r3c9=r6c8]).
      → color(r3c6) = color(r8c8). Identify.
  3.  SET: {row 8, row 9} − {box 7, box 8}.
      Remainder: {[r3c6=r8c8]} = {r7c6}.
      → color([r3c6=r8c8]) = color(r7c6), but they share a house. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:

  1.  SET: {row 8, row 9} − {box 7, box 8}.
      Remainder: {r9c9} = {r7c6}.
      → color(r9c9) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r3c8, r3c6, r3c9, [r7c6=r9c9]} (spine r3c6—r3c9).

      Bivalue oddagon {r3c6, r3c9, r5c9, r6c8, r6c6} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Diamond {r3c9, [r3c6=r9c5], r3c8, r9c8} (spine [r3c6=r9c5]—r3c8).

      Satellites r7c6 (rung 1), r5c9 (rung 2), r6c3 (rung 3) forced to distinct colors. Add triangle.

      Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
      but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Diagonals: {r3c8, r8c9} and {r3c9, r9c8} (non-adjacent).

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

pattern 585/832: PROVED cells=13 depth=1 diamonds=1 odd_wheels=0 circular_ladders=0 bridged_hexagons=1 set_equivalences=0 parity_transports=0 pigeonhole_xwings=0 branches=0 complete=true greedy_branches=0 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=0 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=0 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0
000000000000000000000001011000000000000001000001010001000000000001000101001001010
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r8c3, r8c7, r8c9, r9c8} (spine r8c7—r8c9).
      → color(r8c3) = color(r9c8). Identify.
  2.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r3c6, r3c9, r6c9, r6c3, r9c3, r9c6}
      Bridges: r3c8—[r8c3=r9c8] (edges r3c6—r3c9 ↔ r6c3—r9c3), r8c9—[r8c3=r9c8] (edges r3c9—r6c9 ↔ r9c3—r9c6), r6c5—r5c6 (edges r6c9—r6c3 ↔ r9c6—r3c6).
      Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
      but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Diamond {r6c8, [r6c3=r9c2], r9c8, r9c9} (spine [r6c3=r9c2]—r9c8).

      → color(r3c6) = color([r6c8=r9c9]). Identify.

      Bivalue oddagon {r3c8, r3c9, r5c9, r5c6, r6c5, [r6c3=r9c2], r9c8} (length 7) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r8c3, r8c8, r8c9, r9c7} (spine r8c8—r8c9).
      → color(r8c3) = color(r9c7). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r5c3, [r8c3=r9c7], r9c3, r9c6} (spine [r8c3=r9c7]—r9c3).
      → color(r5c3) = color(r9c6). Identify.
  3.  SET: {row 3, row 6} − {col 6, col 9}.
      Remainder: {r3c8, r6c2} = {[r5c3=r9c6], r8c9}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c8, r3c9, r6c9, r6c2}:
      Diagonals: {r3c8, r6c9} and {r3c9, r6c2} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r3c8) = color(r6c9) → forces r3c8 = r8c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r3c9) = color(r6c2) → forces [r5c3=r9c6] = r6c2 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Diamond {r8c6, r9c4, r9c5, r9c3} (spine r9c4—r9c5).

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → color(r3c6) = color(r8c5). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r3c3, [r3c6=r8c5], r3c9, r8c9} (spine [r3c6=r8c5]—r3c9).
      → color(r3c3) = color(r8c9). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r7c8, [r3c3=r8c9], r9c7, r9c3} (spine [r3c3=r8c9]—r9c7).
      → color(r7c8) = color(r9c3). Identify.
  4.  Diamond {r6c5, r6c3, r6c8, [r7c8=r9c3]} (spine r6c3—r6c8).
      → color(r6c5) = color([r7c8=r9c3]). Identify.
  5.  K₄ on {[r3c6=r8c5], [r6c5=r7c8=r9c3], r7c6, r9c6}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  1.  Diamond {r5c9, r6c7, r6c8, r6c6} (spine r6c7—r6c8).

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

pattern 710/832: PROVED cells=13 depth=1 diamonds=0 odd_wheels=0 circular_ladders=0 bridged_hexagons=1 set_equivalences=1 parity_transports=0 pigeonhole_xwings=0 branches=0 complete=true greedy_branches=0 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=0 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=0 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0
000000000000000000001001001000000000000000010000001011000000000001001010011000001
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {row 3, row 6, row 8, row 9} − {col 3, col 6, col 8, col 9}.
      Remainder: {r9c2} = {r5c8}.
      → color(r9c2) = color(r5c8). Identify.
  2.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r3c6, r3c9, r6c9, [r5c8=r9c2], r8c3, r8c6}
      Bridges: r3c3—r9c3 (edges r3c6—r3c9 ↔ [r5c8=r9c2]—r8c3), r9c9—r8c8 (edges r3c9—r6c9 ↔ r8c3—r8c6), r6c8—r6c6 (edges r6c9—[r5c8=r9c2] ↔ r8c6—r3c6).
      Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
      but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r6c6, r6c9, [r8c3=r9c9], r8c6}:
      Diagonals: {r6c6, [r8c3=r9c9]} and {r6c9, r8c6} (non-adjacent).

Proof of non-3-colorability:

  1.  SET: {row 8, row 9} − {box 7, box 8}.
      Remainder: {r9c8} = {r7c6}.
      → color(r9c8) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  2.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r7c6=r9c8], r8c5, r8c3, r9c2}:
      Diagonals: {[r7c6=r9c8], r8c3} and {r8c5, r9c2} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r7c6=r9c8]) = color(r8c3) → forces r6c8 = [r7c6=r9c8] (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c5) = color(r9c2) → forces r3c3 = r3c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      Satellites r3c9 (rung 1), r6c8 (rung 2) forced to distinct colors. Add edge.
  3.  K₄ on {r3c9, r4c9, r5c9, r6c8}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  4.  Odd wheel: hub [r6c5=r9c8] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {[r3c8=r5c9], r5c6, r9c6, [r6c3=r9c2], r6c8} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

000000000000000001000000011000000000000011001001001000001000000001000000010001010
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r3c8, r2c9, r3c9, r5c9} (spine r2c9—r3c9).
      → color(r3c8) = color(r5c9). Identify.
  2.  SET: {col 3, col 6} − {box 5, box 7}.
      Remainder: {r6c3, r9c6} = {r5c5, r9c2}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r3c8=r5c9], r5c5, r9c2, r9c8}:
      Diagonals: {[r3c8=r5c9], r9c2} and {r5c5, r9c8} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r3c8=r5c9]) = color(r9c2) → forces r6c3 = r6c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r5c5) = color(r9c8) → forces r5c5 = r6c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {row 3, row 6} − {box 3, box 5}.
      Remainder: {r3c6, r6c8} = {r2c9, r5c6}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  2.  SET: {row 6, row 9} − {box 5, box 7}.
      Remainder: {r6c8, r9c6} = {r5c6, r8c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r2c9, r5c6, r8c3, r8c9}:
      Diagonals: {r2c9, r8c3} and {r5c6, r8c9} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r2c9) = color(r8c3) → forces r3c6 = r9c6 (adjacent). Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r5c6) = color(r8c9) → forces r3c8 = r6c8 (adjacent). Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r2c9, r3c7, r3c8, r3c6} (spine r3c7—r3c8).
      → color(r2c9) = color(r3c6). Identify.
  2.  SET: {row 3, row 6, row 9} − {box 3, box 5, box 7}.
      Remainder: {[r2c9=r3c6], r6c3, r9c9} = {[r2c9=r3c6], r5c6, r8c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  K₄ on {[r2c9=r3c6], r5c6, r8c3, r8c6}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □
